  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_0821a3ae-e357-4abc-9b79-1055d45ee5d4'
      });

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer12997878887955521947">Never trust your heart to the New York Times bestselling master of suspense, Stephen King. Especially with an anthology that features the classic stories "Children of the Corn," "The Lawnmower Man," "Graveyard Shift," "The Mangler," and "Sometimes They Come Back"-which were all made into hit horror films.<br/><br/>From the depths of darkness, where hideous rats defend their empire, </span>
  <span id="freeText12997878887955521947" style="display:none">Never trust your heart to the New York Times bestselling master of suspense, Stephen King. Especially with an anthology that features the classic stories "Children of the Corn," "The Lawnmower Man," "Graveyard Shift," "The Mangler," and "Sometimes They Come Back"-which were all made into hit horror films.<br /><br />From the depths of darkness, where hideous rats defend their empire, to dizzying heights, where a beautiful girl hangs by a hair above a hellish fate, this chilling collection of twenty short stories will plunge readers into the subterranean labyrinth of the most spine-tingling, eerie imagination of our time.<br /><br />Contents:<br /><br />· Introduction · John D. MacDonald · in <br />· Foreword · fw <br />· Jerusalem’s Lot · nv Night Shift, Garden City, NY: Doubleday, 1978 <br />· Graveyard Shift · ss Cavalier Oct ’70 <br />· Night Surf · ss Cavalier Aug ’74 <br />· I Am the Doorway · ss Cavalier Mar ’71 <br />· The Mangler · nv Cavalier Dec ’72 <br />· The Boogeyman · ss Cavalier Mar ’73 <br />· Gray Matter · ss Cavalier Oct ’73 <br />· Battleground · ss Cavalier Sep ’72 <br />· Trucks · ss Cavalier Jun ’73 <br />· Sometimes They Come Back · nv Cavalier Mar ’74 <br />· Strawberry Spring · ss Ubris Fll ’68; Cavalier Nov ’75 <br />· The Ledge · ss Penthouse Jul ’76 <br />· The Lawnmower Man · ss Cavalier May ’75 <br />· Quitters, Inc. · ss Night Shift, Garden City, NY: Doubleday, 1978 <br />· I Know What You Need · nv Cosmopolitan Sep ’76 <br />· Children of the Corn · nv Penthouse Mar ’77 <br />· The Last Rung on the Ladder · ss Night Shift, Garden City, NY: Doubleday, 1978 <br />· The Man Who Loved Flowers · ss Gallery Aug ’77 <br />· One for the Road · ss Maine Mar ’77 <br />· The Woman in the Room · ss Night Shift, Garden City, NY: Doubleday, 1978</span>

<div id="review_82972736" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/82972736" />
    <a title="Wil Wheaton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2040005-wil-wheaton"><img alt="Wil Wheaton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356706506p2/2040005.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/82972736?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wil Wheaton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wil Wheaton" href="/user/show/2040005-wil-wheaton">Wil Wheaton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2040005-wil-wheaton?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer82972736" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13810290363809877906">I reread this book, because I'm about to start working on my own collection of short stories, and I wanted to reconnect to the book that inspired me to be a writer, 35 years ago.<br/><br/>I enjoyed it so much more as an adult than I did as a kid, because I have lived more and have more of my own experiences to relate to the stories, characters, and experiences in the different chapters.<br/><br/>But the thing I loved the most about this was how much it inspired me to write my own stories, and how much it reminded m</span>
  <span id="freeText13810290363809877906" style="display:none">I reread this book, because I'm about to start working on my own collection of short stories, and I wanted to reconnect to the book that inspired me to be a writer, 35 years ago.<br /><br />I enjoyed it so much more as an adult than I did as a kid, because I have lived more and have more of my own experiences to relate to the stories, characters, and experiences in the different chapters.<br /><br />But the thing I loved the most about this was how much it inspired me to write my own stories, and how much it reminded me about plot, structure, and narrative in stories that are about 5000 words, each.<br /><br />Really glad I read this again. Thanks, Stephen King!</span>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_500804566" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/500804566" />
    <a title="Matthew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew"><img alt="Matthew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464987365p2/16254355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/500804566?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew">Matthew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780451160454" href="/book/show/155415.Night_Shift">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=monsters">monsters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=read-more-than-once">read-more-than-once</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=supernatural">supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=stephen-king">stephen-king</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer500804566" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9445643282780824313">King's first short story collection comes in at 4.125 stars. As you can see below, I rated and reviewed each story. Then, I added all the ratings together and took the average to get my overall rating. <br/><br/>This was my second time through and better than I remembered. A few stories that could be skipped, but you might as well read them all to get the full experience!<br/><br/>************************<br/><br/><b>Jerusalem's Lot - 4.5 stars</b><br/>And earlier story of the same town and environs found in the novel 'Salem's Lot. Writ</span>
  <span id="freeText9445643282780824313" style="display:none">King's first short story collection comes in at 4.125 stars. As you can see below, I rated and reviewed each story. Then, I added all the ratings together and took the average to get my overall rating. <br><br>This was my second time through and better than I remembered. A few stories that could be skipped, but you might as well read them all to get the full experience!<br><br>************************<br><br><b>Jerusalem's Lot - 4.5 stars</b><br>And earlier story of the same town and environs found in the novel 'Salem's Lot. Written in a style - letters and journal entries - that reminded me a lot of horror classics like Dracula and Frankenstein. This is a nice little taste of demonic shenanigans and eerie foreshadowing. A great way to start off a short story collection!<br><br><b>Graveyard Shift - 5 stars</b><br>Time for some spring cleaning! Nature is crazy sometimes. Your boss can be a jerk sometimes. Combine the two and you get this terrifying story of revenge. I spent most of the time cringing!<br><br><b>Night Surf - 2.5 stars</b><br>Not bad, but not really a full story. As it takes place in the world from The Stand, it feels more like a writing exercise that King used to help build the bigger story. Or, maybe an anecdote he was thinking about including, but pulled it out of the final product. Without knowing the backstory of The Stand, I am not sure this story will mean much to a reader.<br><br><b>I Am The Doorway - 5 stars</b><br>This story explains the cover of the edition I am reading. Great horror sci-fi. King does a great job jamming a lot of content in ten pages or so. I also love it when the very last sentence of a story hits just as hard as the whole rest of the story. Awesome stuff here!<br><br><b>The Mangler - 5 stars</b><br>More demonic possession - I am sensing a theme here! I am pretty sure that most King fans consider this short story one of his classics. It led to a series of what I am sure are very cheesy horror movies. I never saw them, but I have read this short story many times and I know that I love it!<br><br><b>The Boogeyman - 4 stars</b><br>This is an allegorical tale about a racist, sexist, generally unpleasant man who is willing to judge others but cannot see his own faults. But, you can't hide from the boogeyman!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1556026356ra/27402510.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Gray Matter - 4 stars</b><br>Does this taste a little bit off to you? In an age of e-coli and biohazard scares, this story will play off your fears about what might be out there waiting to get you from the inside out. 10 out of 10 on the gross meter!<br><br><b>Battleground - 5 stars</b><br>Definitely one of my top 5 favorite Stephen King short stories. Probably the best King ending of any of his stories. This story is short but sweet and worth reading even if you don't read the rest of the book.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1556250705ra/27414990.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Trucks - 5 stars</b><br>The basis for King's only directorial endeavor, the classic Maximum Overdrive (yeah, I said classic! FIGHT ME!) They also made another movie based on it, but I am not sure why. What if all those semis on the interstate took over? Maybe they're mad? There is a nostalgic place in my heart for this story!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1556331192ra/27419652.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Sometimes They Come Back - 3.5 stars</b><br>You guessed it - demons again! This was the longest short story so far in the collection. When reading short stories I feel like they have to be crafted perfectly to get in, get out, BOOM! You end up blown away in just a few words. While I enjoyed this one, I think it rambled on just a little bit too long and the end was probably the least shocking of any so far in the book.<br><br><b>Strawberry Spring - 4 stars</b><br>I like the story telling in this one a lot. I also think is is interesting how the rumor mill and media twisting of stories we see today was just as big of an issue back in the 1970s; everyone had a different take and everyone believed it 100%. A bit of a cheesy twist at the end, but overall, not bad!<br><br><b>The Ledge - 5 stars</b><br>This is another short story favorite of mine. Also, this is one that made its way to the big screen in the 80s classic Cat's Eye. No demons or monsters in this one, just humans pushing morality and fear to the limit in the name of money and pride."<br><br><b>The Lawnmower Man - 3 stars</b><br>I remember reading this story a long time ago and it is always what I think of when I think of King short stories that I do not like quite as much as the others. It is just out there; kind of creepy, but not super enthralling (to me). They also (for some reason) made a terrible movie based on this that was mainly just the same title.<br><br><b>Quitters, Inc. - 5 stars</b><br>Another classic King short story and probably one of his most well known. Like the previously discussed story, The Ledge, this is also one featured in the 80's King movie Cat's Eye. The plot of this one is just so oddly cool and the means to an end so logically maniacal that you can't help but say "That's f#%$ed up! But, kinda makes sense!"<br><br><b>I Know What You Need - 4 stars</b><br>Stephen King's version of the movie What Women Want. But, of course, it isn't a comedy!<br><br><b>Children of the Corn - 4.5 stars</b><br>Kids can be super creepy! You won't taking driving through the country-side for granted after this one. This is another classic King that I think most people have heard of. Also, I believe it has led to more movies than any other King story or novel. I just checked and there have been 10 - the earliest in 1984, the most recent in 2018.<br><br><b>The Last Rung on the Ladder - 2 stars</b><br>Meh. Not a bad story, but just kinda doesn't feel right in the context of this book. So far, my least favorite in this collection.<br><br><b>The Man Who Loved Flowers - 4.5 stars</b><br>Now that is an awesome way to tell a whole story in 6 pages. Well executed and mysterious. To be blunt, young love can be painful!<br><br><b>One for the Road - 4.5 stars</b><br>We've been here before . . . many times . . . and we will definitely go here again someday. But, whenever we go, evil is sure to follow. A very creepy sequel!<br><br><b>The Woman in the Room - 2.5 stars</b><br>As my mother is in a nursing home, I struggled a bit with this one. Kind of an unexpected end to this collection. I think it would have done better to end on the story before this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9445643282780824313" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3589006449" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9023810393929664364">4.5 Stars ⭐️ <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1600260980ra/30113968.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>1. <div id="review_23740788" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/23740788" />
    <a title="Fabian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1036893-fabian"><img alt="Fabian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514061293p2/1036893.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/23740788?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fabian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fabian" href="/user/show/1036893-fabian">Fabian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780451131317" href="/book/show/1278424.Night_Shift">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">REAL hardcore S. King fans</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer23740788" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10085704587876723822">These are short stories (though not truly novellas) which actually serve as delectable intros to popular King mythologies (for a staggering example see [or better yet, don't {with the exception of "Trucks" a.k.a. "Maximum Overdrive" for B-level entertainment and "Children of the Corn" with its quaint moments of childlike chills}] all the movies made from like eight of these tales.) Here, King is at his most bizarre, most morbid. Most of his part-time heroes & (just a few) heroines, end up dead o</span>
  <span id="freeText10085704587876723822" style="display:none">These are short stories (though not truly novellas) which actually serve as delectable intros to popular King mythologies (for a staggering example see [or better yet, don't {with the exception of "Trucks" a.k.a. "Maximum Overdrive" for B-level entertainment and "Children of the Corn" with its quaint moments of childlike chills}] all the movies made from like eight of these tales.) Here, King is at his most bizarre, most morbid. Most of his part-time heroes &amp; (just a few) heroines, end up dead or suffering the loss of a child, wife, mother. Sometimes one story seems to bleed onto another one by motif (corn... rats... snow... death machines... death [duh]). The editing I must admit is masterful. The most avant-garde stories bookend it nicely; it even makes reference to 'Salem's Lot, one book I must admit I still have to read, and there are comical undertones &amp; some misogynist parts (!!!!). I love how un-Stephen King this is, for someone who's used to being satisfied with around 78% of his work.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10085704587876723822" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1123990157" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1123990157" />
    <a title="Will M." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20408288-will-m"><img alt="Will M." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452951660p2/20408288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1123990157?book_show_action=true">Dec 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Will M." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Will M." href="/user/show/20408288-will-m">Will M.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/9808780-night-shift">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1123990157" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer31407336742905845">Also posted at my blog: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://killerscorpion.wordpress.com/2015/02/14/night-shift-by-stephen-king/'>https://killerscorpion.wordpress.com/...</a><br/><br/>I find it really difficult to review short stories, especially anthologies. Night Shift is a collection of King's short stories, and if I'm not mistaken, this is a collection of the first short stories he wrote in his early years of writing. The most shocking thing you have to know is that the writing is not outdated. That's the thing about King, I've read his first book <u> Carrie </u> and the writing of it still felt like he wrote it mon</span>
  <span id="freeText31407336742905845" style="display:none">Also posted at my blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://killerscorpion.wordpress.com/2015/02/14/night-shift-by-stephen-king/">https://killerscorpion.wordpress.com/...</a><br /><br />I find it really difficult to review short stories, especially anthologies. Night Shift is a collection of King's short stories, and if I'm not mistaken, this is a collection of the first short stories he wrote in his early years of writing. The most shocking thing you have to know is that the writing is not outdated. That's the thing about King, I've read his first book <u> Carrie </u> and the writing of it still felt like he wrote it months ago. Amazing author indeed.<br /><br />I'm unsure of what to write here. It would make this review damn long if I were to review each short story, so I'll just list down my favorites, and not so favorites, then give a brief explanation why I liked/disliked it. The ones not mentioned were either likable or boring. <br /><br />The likes: <br /><u>Graveyard Shift</u><br />Something about mutated rats really caught my interest. I'm not normally afraid of rats, but if ever I see one as big as the ones described in this short story, then I would probably be scared as hell.<br /><br /><u>Night Surf</u><br />The basis for The Stand, which is one of my favorites novels of all time. It was short but quite satisfying. I liked how King introduced the disease that would cause so much havoc in The Stand.<br /><br /><u>Quitter's Inc</u><br />Honestly it would be a sin not to like this. No spoilers along your way though, so all I can say is choose your decisions wisely. It has been proven how addictive smoking is. I've never smoked in my life, and after reading this, I don't think I ever will. The plot presented here is not unlikely to happen in real life, and that's the reason why this was so scary and entertaining at the same time.<br /><br /><u> The Woman In The Room</u><br />Originality might not be the most prominent factor of this short story, but it was executed quite nicely. I liked the main character and it was a satisfying short read.<br /><br /><u>Sometimes They Come Back</u><br />Please don't let them come back. The main character here was really likable, and the supernatural element was creepy as fuck. Good thing I was reading this one in the afternoon. A bit scarier than Pet Sematary if one were to look at the bigger picture.<br /><br /><u>The Ledge</u><br />Who doesn't like to read about gambling/bets? I sure do. The deceiver becomes the deceived.<br /><br /><u>I Know What You Need</u><br />Creepy as fuck if ever I meet a woman of the same kind as the weird man in this one. For me this tackled psychological factors with a pinch of supernatural element/s along the way. Typical King. Amazing.<br /><br />and last, my favorite of them all, <u>The Boogeyman </u><br />I read The Boogeyman at one in the morning. That was the worst decision I've ever made in my reading life, so far (maybe alongside Pet Sematary). This one was fucking scary I had to turn on the lights right after. As none of you know, I'm a bit of a nocturnal person. I'm most productive at night, and being a Stephen King fan doesn't really bode well with the nocturnal life. Really likable characters that were fully developed despite this being a short story. The Boogeyman was fucking scary and the ending scared me the most. The best of the whole collection.<br /><br />There are the ones that I disliked. I don't think I should do an "in-depth" review of them anymore because the ones that I did like managed to make this review long already. Let me just comment on how much I hated <u> Jerusalem's Lot </u> but really liked <u> One for The Road </u>. Both are related to 'Salem's Lot, a novel that I really didn't like. I was expecting to like JL so that I could have a better reread of 'Salem's Lot in the future, but nope, I hated it just as much. Another noteworthy disappointment would be <u> Gray Matter </u>. I'm sure it was showcased at the back of the book for a reason, but I'm quite unsure of what that reason would be. <br /><br />4.5/5 stars. Not a perfect collection but some will never be forgotten. This collection was executed beautifully considering this was written in King's early writing years. There's a reason why King is my favorite author, and most of his works prove my point. This is one of those works. Read this if you want to be scared, and I'd recommend reading this at night.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="31407336742905845" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1113330792" />
    <a title="Edward Lorn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn"><img alt="Edward Lorn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492199506p2/8850418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1113330792?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward Lorn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward Lorn" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn">Edward Lorn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780451099310" href="/book/show/155619.Night_Shift">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1113330792" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2416617064527383456">First read this collection when I was... twenty, I think. Not sure. Does it matter? Probably not. Three things to mention before hitting you with my one sentence reviews: I forgot how much of King's early work tied into these stories, and how much I enjoyed his non-horror outings. Truth be told, I probably didn't like the more literary stories that I read once upon a when because I was a tried and true idiot in those days (I'm still an idiot, but my wife turned me into a functioning idiot, and I</span>
  <span id="freeText2416617064527383456" style="display:none">First read this collection when I was... twenty, I think. Not sure. Does it matter? Probably not. Three things to mention before hitting you with my one sentence reviews: I forgot how much of King's early work tied into these stories, and how much I enjoyed his non-horror outings. Truth be told, I probably didn't like the more literary stories that I read once upon a when because I was a tried and true idiot in those days (I'm still an idiot, but my wife turned me into a functioning idiot, and I say thankee sai). Finally, this is probably the most fun anyone will ever have with a King collection. There are stories in here that are simply fucking cool. The concepts are fun, even if they are a tad bit violent, but there's a heaping helping of humor to go along with the sadness and the terror. I don't think any other collection, novella, or novel of his can match the sheer entertainment factor of this, his first published collection. You might disagree; and if you do, give some examples in the comment section. Once again, I know there's scarier and more moving stories of his out there, but do you think any of them are thing much fun? <br /><br />On with the single-sentence reviews:<br /><br />"Jerusalem's Lot" - King's first attempt at Lovecraft fan fiction is a three-star outing for me because of the epistolary style, which I don't like.<br /><br />"Graveyard Shift" - Four stars worth of nasty fun that shows King's not opposed to the time-tested rule of get in, get dirty, and get out.<br /><br />"Night Surf" - A four-star jaunt back into a Captain Trips-ravaged world that I dug quite a bit.<br /><br />"I am the Doorway" - A tasty tidbit of sci fi horror that gets under your skin and explains that the cover you see above is quite literal in this four-star outing.<br /><br />"The Mangler" - Five demon-possessed pieces of industrial laundry equipment out of five for being the goriest thing I've read all year. <br /><br />"Grey Matter" - I'm going deeper into this one. I believe this story was the catalyst to great many things in the King-verse. The "Grays" from Tommyknockers and Dreamcatcher make an appearance, as well as a little story about a man going into a Bangor sewer to find a giant spider. The man comes out with his hair white as snow, and dies two years later, crazy as a shithouse rat. Of course these are only my theories, but I'm giving this story five stars based on possible coolness factor alone.<br /><br />"Battleground" - Ten pages and four star's worth of big fun that any kid who's ever played with little green army men will enjoy. <br /><br />"Trucks" - Three stars for the story that inspired the movie Maximum Overdrive, that B-movie masterpiece penned by King himself. <br /><br />"Sometimes They Come Back" - Two stars for this predictable little ditty that never has struck the right chord with me.<br /><br />"Strawberry Spring" - This five-star number is probably up there in my top ten Stephen King shorts; short stories, not the man's knickers. <br /><br />"The Ledge" - A different kind of three-star thriller that makes me wonder why King has written two tales (the novel Cujo, and this seventeen-page story) about a woman who has an affair with her tennis instructor. <br /><br />"The Lawnmower Man" - This two-star pile of offal was turned into a movie so horrible, King himself requested his name be stricken from the credits, but the story was just as bad as the movie, even though neither one had shit to do with the other.<br /><br />"Quitters, Inc" - I honestly cannot believe that the same man who wrote "The Lawnmower Man" wrote "Quitters, Inc.", because this five-star tale of willpower and familial love is altogether a horse of a different color.<br /><br />"I Know What You Need" - This three-star read first appeared in Cosmopolitan, and that's all I have to say about that.<br /><br />"Children of the Corn" - My favorite story in this collection easily gets all the stars, because kids and corn are scary, yo!<br /><br />"The Last Rung on the Ladder" - Well that one was a mule kick to the feels, so I guess it gets all the stars too.<br /><br />"The Man Who Loves Flowers" - Gets four stars based on nostalgia factor alone, as I believe it's the first short story of King's that I ever sampled. <br /><br />"One for the Road" - The second to last story in this collection gets four stars simply for being a companion to 'Salem's Lot.<br /><br />"The Woman in the Room" - Is an emotionally driven four-star effort that hits a little too close to home for me.<br /><br />Notable names:<br /><br />This time around, King references his other books in multiple ways, but mostly by the towns that would come to host some of his most famous works. Below you will find a list of these towns, and any names that struck a chord with me.<br /><br />Hemingford Home<br />Derry<br />Jerusalem's Lot<br />Gates Falls<br />Haven<br /><br />Patrick Hockstetter (this name pops up all throughout the King-verse, but I don't think it's the same person every time, mainly because, when he's just a teen, Hockstetter dies at the hands of Pennywise, yet he goes on to write a book that's referenced in Carrie then becomes a scientist in Firestarter.)<br /><br />In summation: Probably the most fun you will have with Stephen King. From animated army men to great beasts that tromp behind the rows, this collection is sure to please. Highly ecommended.<br /><br />(Author's note: I said I wouldn't be doing his collections during my massive reread of King's catalog, but I'm well ahead of schedule, so here you go. I plan on doing a decade of Kingly works every three months. I started in October, and have read everything he published between 1974 and 1984. Aside from Different Seasons, I'm all caught up with that time period. I think I'll do the audio books of those next...)</span>
  <a data-text-id="2416617064527383456" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2460702271" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2460702271" />
    <a title="Erin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32799998-erin"><img alt="Erin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1469767858p2/32799998.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2460702271?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/32799998-erin">Erin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780451011022" href="/book/show/155511.Night_Shift">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32799998-erin?shelf=king-me">king-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32799998-erin?shelf=july-2018">july-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2460702271" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18190987791240528744">As I continue my Stephen King binge, I seem to be leaning more towards his short story collections. As I've said before Stephen King is one of the best short story writers around. <br/><br/><br/>Night Shift was a bit of a mixed bag but there were way more great stories then bad ones.<br/><br/>My favorite stories were The Boogeyman in which a man learns to keep he's closet doors closed, Grey Matter in which we all learn that beer is bad, Sometimes They Come Back in which a teacher finds out that you can't out run your pa</span>
  <span id="freeText18190987791240528744" style="display:none">As I continue my Stephen King binge, I seem to be leaning more towards his short story collections. As I've said before Stephen King is one of the best short story writers around. <br /><br /><br />Night Shift was a bit of a mixed bag but there were way more great stories then bad ones.<br /><br />My favorite stories were The Boogeyman in which a man learns to keep he's closet doors closed, Grey Matter in which we all learn that beer is bad, Sometimes They Come Back in which a teacher finds out that you can't out run your past, Quitters, Inc. in which a man learns that he should have read the fine print, Children of the Corn kids are monsters and corn is important, and The Man Who Loved Flowers in which we meet a young man who won't give up on love. <br /><br />I really only had 3 stories I disliked: Number 1 was The Lawnmower Man I don't even want to talk about it. It was awful<br /> Number 2: Trucks, so boring.<br />Number 3 : Graveyard Shift, damn RATS! <br /><br />Night Shift is a vintage read and some stories are super dated but as I said before there are more great and timeless stories in this collection then there are clunkers. <br /><br />No rec. Either you like Stephen King or you don't.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18190987791240528744" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1016772381" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1016772381" />
    <a title="Alejandro" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro"><img alt="Alejandro" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328672389p2/665584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1016772381?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alejandro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alejandro" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro">Alejandro</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781444723199" href="/book/show/11247977-night-shift">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=horror">horror</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=anthology">anthology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1016772381" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10729191407336954124"><b>
  <u>Stephen King’s first anthology!</u>
</b><br/><br/><br/><i>The general rating is an average result of each individual rating of the stories contained in the anthology.</i><br/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>JERUSALEM’S LOT</u>
</b><br/><br/>Rating: *** ( 3 stars )<br/><br/>This is a short story which serves as an introductory prequel if you later wanted to read <i>Salem’s Lot</i> novel. <br/><br/>Set in 1850, Charles Boones inherited the Chapelwaite manor, which is feared by the people of Preacher’s Corners town, and that has a dark connection with Jerusalem’s Lot, a deserted village, quite near of </span>
  <span id="freeText10729191407336954124" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>Stephen King’s first anthology!</u>
</b><br /><br /><br /><i>The general rating is an average result of each individual rating of the stories contained in the anthology.</i><br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>JERUSALEM’S LOT</u>
</b><br /><br />Rating: *** ( 3 stars )<br /><br />This is a short story which serves as an introductory prequel if you later wanted to read <i>Salem’s Lot</i> novel. <br /><br />Set in 1850, Charles Boones inherited the Chapelwaite manor, which is feared by the people of Preacher’s Corners town, and that has a dark connection with Jerusalem’s Lot, a deserted village, quite near of the manor. When you started to hear something inside the walls…<br /><br />…it’s the beginning of the end.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>GRAVEYARD SHIFT</u>
</b><br /><br />Rating: **** ( 4 stars )<br /><br />During the holiday weekend of Fourth of July, in a mill, it’s offered to several employees to get an extra bonus for cleaning a very old basement that it hasn’t been cleaned for 12 years…<br /><br />…obviously there are rats, but oddly there aren’t as much as you may expect…<br /><br />…where have gone the rest of them?<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>NIGHT SURF</u>
</b><br /><br />Rating: * ( 1 stars )<br /><br />A bunch of awful teenagers go to the beach at night, in the middle of an apocalyptical world where the most of population have died due a contagious decease.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>I AM THE DOORWAY</u>
</b><br /><br />Rating: **** ( 4 stars )<br /><br />In a parallel reality where the NASA space program was able not only reaching the Moon, but also Mars, during a mission to Venus, one of the astronauts suffered an accident, losing the ability to walk, but got in his hands a very twisted and dangerous ability instead.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE MANGLER</u>
</b><br /><br />Rating: ***** ( 5 stars )<br /><br />In an industrial laundry facility, due an odd series of coincidences, a speed ironer machine tasted blood…<br /><br />…and it liked it.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE BOOGEYMAN</u>
</b><br /><br />Rating: ***** ( 5 stars )<br /><br />A man goes to the psychiatrist to talk out his strange and deadly past experiences that caused the death of all his children…<br /><br />…and never lose of sight the closet’s door.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>GRAY MATTER</u>
</b><br /><br />Rating: ** ( 2 stars )<br /><br />A kid arrived to a bar, and one of the customers offered to take him back to his appartment, where his odd dad is wating.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>BATTLEGROUND</u>
</b><br /><br />Rating: *** ( 3 stars )<br /><br />A profesional hitman suffered the revenge of a toyman whom he killed.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>TRUCKS</u>
</b><br /><br />Rating: **** ( 4 stars )<br /><br />Madness is unleashed in a gas station when trucks and semi-trailers got alive and started to kill any human around, until a small bunch of survivors got trapped in the dinner, part of the gas station facility.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>SOMETIMES THEY COME BACK</u>
</b><br /><br />Rating: ***** ( 5 stars )<br /><br />Two young brothers cross fates with a gang of punks, and after one of the brothers died, the other escapes. Years later, the surviving brother got married and became an English teacher…<br /><br />…however, after Xmas break, his students started to die, while getting odd replacement students.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>STRAWBERRY SPRING</u>
</b><br /><br />Rating: ***** ( 5 stars )<br /><br />During a “strawberry spring”, a kind of false mini season, provoking fog at nights, perfect ambiance for a serial killer’s murdering spree at New Sharon College…<br /><br />…the Springheel Jack killer is loose!<br /><br />Several students are murdered and panic is everywhere at the New Sharon College.<br /><br />Eight years later, the “strawberry spring” is back, the fog is back, and…<br /><br />…the Sprinheel Jack killer is back!<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE LEDGE</u>
</b><br /><br />Rating: **** ( 4 stars )<br /><br />Something that you shouldn’t do is having an affair with the wife of a criminal lord…<br /><br />…and other thing that you shouldn’t try is playing odd bets.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE LAWNMOWER MAN</u>
</b><br /><br />Rating: ***** ( 5 stars )<br /><br />There is a successful lawnmowing company, however, none client has ever being able to see who s the owner of it, one of the clients decided to take a peek and found out the mystery…<br /><br />…but there are mystery beyond your wildest nightmares and they should remain unknown.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>QUITTERS, INC.</u>
</b><br /><br />Rating: ***** ( 5 stars )<br /><br />Some people say that habits are nasty things…<br /><br />…but sometimes, quitting those habits can be even nastier things…<br /><br />…not only for the addict…<br /><br />…but his/her family too.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>I KNOW WHAT YOU NEED</u>
</b><br /><br />Rating: *** ( 3 stars )<br /><br />In war and love, everything goes…<br /><br />…but there should be limits for some used stuff.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>CHILDREN OF THE CORN</u>
</b><br /><br />Rating: ***** ( 5 stars )<br /><br />Vicky and Burt, are a troubling married couple, doing a road trip through the heart of the United States, hoping to save their fragile marriage. However, when they are traveling alongside of a massive cornfield, they hit a boy with their car, but when they checked the body, they noticed that they boy had his throat already sliced and he was almost dead when hit. <br /><br />They opted to take the kid’s body to the nearest town which the map says is Gatlin, but when they arrived there, it’s a ghost town and everything seemed to stop 12 years ago…<br /><br />…however, the town isn’t as deserted as it seemed…<br /><br />…and zealot kids isn’t the only thing that they should be afraid about.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE LAST RUNG ON THE LADDER</u>
</b><br /><br />Rating: **** ( 4 stars )<br /><br />Heart-breaking tale of two sibbings (brother and sister) and how their strong connection when they were kids was getting weaker and weaker, meanwhile they got older and their paths took separate but kinda of similarly depressing fates.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE MAN WHO LOVED FLOWERS</u>
</b><br /><br />Rating: **** ( 4 stars )<br /><br />Love is in the air, but so is murder, and the fateful date of a man with the woman who loves will turn into a tragedy.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>ONE FOR THE ROAD</u>
</b><br /><br />Rating: *** ( 3 stars )<br /><br />This is a short story which serves as a sequel for the <i>Salem’s Lot</i> novel.<br /><br />Set a couple of years later of the events of <i>Salem’s Lot</i>, in a bar, two men decided to venture into a deadly blizzard to try to save a family stranded just in the middle of the dreadful Jerusalem’s Lot village.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE WOMAN IN THE ROOM</u>
</b><br /><br />Rating: *** ( 3 stars )<br /><br />Remorse and guilt overwhelm to a troubling man after deciding to end the suffering of his unhealthy mother.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10729191407336954124" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1443203843" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1443203843" />
    <a title="Fabian {Councillor}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40792319-fabian-councillor"><img alt="Fabian {Councillor}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599133151p2/40792319.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1443203843?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fabian {Councillor}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fabian {Councillor}" href="/user/show/40792319-fabian-councillor">Fabian {Councillor}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/9808780-night-shift">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=year-1978">year-1978</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=stephen-king">stephen-king</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=to-read-2016-priority">to-read-2016-priority</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=short-story-collections">short-story-collections</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40792319-fabian-councillor?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1443203843" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12181343215472795820">Many readers consider this book to be one of Stephen King's most popular short story collections, and I can't disagree with that opinion ... mostly because it's only the second anthology by King I have read so far. Many original horror stories are included in this collection, with most of them having been adapted into classic horror movies like "Children of the Corn", "Graveyard Shift" or "The Mangler". In its entirety, however, I consider "Night Shift" to be a rather weak collection of short st</span>
  <span id="freeText12181343215472795820" style="display:none">Many readers consider this book to be one of Stephen King's most popular short story collections, and I can't disagree with that opinion ... mostly because it's only the second anthology by King I have read so far. Many original horror stories are included in this collection, with most of them having been adapted into classic horror movies like "Children of the Corn", "Graveyard Shift" or "The Mangler". In its entirety, however, I consider "Night Shift" to be a rather weak collection of short stories, and critics will certainly find affirmation that King is also able to write true crap. But on the other hand, some of the best short stories which might be discovered in King's writing universe are included here.<br /><br />In the following, I will list a short overview on the particular stories with my opinions on them. Because well, it's impossible for me to review this collection without taking a look at each of the stories itself, with so many crappy and so many fantastic short stories combined in one book.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>1) Jerusalem's Lot</u>
</b> (2,5/5 stars)<br />The first short story in Stephen King's first anthology deals with the origins of the fictional town Jerusalem's Lot which the reader already knows from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11590._Salem_s_Lot" title="'Salem's Lot by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">'Salem's Lot</a>. However, the story hasn't a lot in common with the novel counterpart, and whoever expects to find the roots of Kurt Barlow and the vampires will end up being disappointed. In epistolary form, Stephen King allows us to take a look at the story of a man called Charles Boone, who inherits the estate Chapelwaite and soon realizes that something with his new residence is not quite the way it should be.<br />Nothing felt particularly outstanding in this story except for the epistolary structure, and as an introduction to the anthology it was a little bit deterring to me.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>2) Graveyard Shift</u>
</b> (3/5 stars)<br />Imagine working in a mill. No light except for electric torches. A bullying foreman who wants you to keep working, no matter what happens. And big, fat rats straying through the mill ...<br />I'll give a piece of advice to you: Don't read this story if you have a rat phobia. Don't read this story if you like your protagonists realistic and without weird changes in behaviour. And definitely don't read this story if you intend to enter a cave or a mill anytime soon. It might not be your wisest idea in those cases.<br />"Graveyard Shift" was a good story with creepy moments, but certainly with too much build-up in the beginning and too much speed in the ending.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>3) Night Surf</u>
</b> (1/5 stars)<br /><i>»Even his big radio/tape-player was hardly more than a nice-looking <u>hunk of junk.</u>«</i> I'll borrow that quote from King's own story and apply it here to describe it. 'Hunk of junk' is actually pretty appropriate. I can't even explain what this story is about because it frustrated and bored me so much.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>4) I am the Doorway</u>
</b> (4/5 stars)<br />A crossover between the genres Horror and Sci-Fi, this story fantastically explores the effects of a confrontation of one human being with alien powers. I was hooked from the beginning and suffered vicariously my way through to the ending along with a hardly remarkable protagonist who turned into an interesting character because of his fate - as, after being exposed to a certain mutagen, tiny eyeballs break out on his fingertips ...<br /><br /><b>
  <u>5) The Mangler</u>
</b> (1/5 stars)<br />Ridiculous attempt to write about a haunted laundry. Let's better forget this story even exists.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>6) The Boogeyman</u>
</b> (3/5 stars)<br />A father who has lost all three of his children to 'the boogeyman' visits a psychiatrist to tell about the terrifying deeds which have been committed against his family.<br />One of the more frightening stories, but certainly also belonging to the more forgettable ones in this collection.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>7) Grey Matter</u>
</b> (1/5 stars)<br />This one just didn't catch my attention or attract my interest. I forgot what it was about ten minutes after reading it. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>8) Battleground</u>
</b> (1/5 stars)<br />I didn't get what this was supposed to be. A man attacked by tiny soldiers one inch and a half big?<br />...<br />Seriously? Was Mr. King on drugs while he wrote this?<br /><br /><b>
  <u>9) Trucks</u>
</b> (1/5 stars)<br />A small town is attacked by haunted trucks, that's the basic essence of this short story. It may be used as the exact definition of ridiculousness. No soul behind these words; no sense behind this plot; no characteristics behind these appearing persons. Just another stupid story to be forgotten.<br /><br /><br />You may think that I was so frustrated after those first nine stories that I was tempted to give up on it? Well, yes, I certainly was. But I kept telling myself to continue, not to abandon this, to believe in the power of King's writing ...<br />And he proved me right.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>10) Sometimes they come back</u>
</b> (3,5/5 stars)<br />In one of the longest stories of the collection, Stephen King explores the life of a teacher for English literature who has been marked by a traumatic event of his past. Now, one after another, new students enter his class. And they look exactly like the teenagers who have attacked and killed his brother - about fifteen years ago ...<br />A very good story with a lot of action, insight and interesting twists and turns. I would have liked to read a full-length novel of this with a more fleshed-out protagonist; the potential was clearly visible. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>11) Strawberry Spring</u>
</b> (4/5 stars)<br />Do you know this feeling when you're reading a mystery and suddenly have an idea on the potential outcome, which is so unlikely you immediately pass it, but then you realize the author has actually chosen this outcome for his story? I experienced it here, and it made me love the story even more. One of King's less-known stories, but definitely a fine piece of writing. The ending can be spoiled so easily that I will not even attempt to give you an idea of what it is about.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>12) The Ledge</u>
</b> <b>(5/5 stars)</b><br />In "The Ledge", a rich man is cheated on by his wife with her tennis instructor. The two men are confronted with each other in the penthouse of a skyscraper. And the husband has to settle a score - he comes up with a plan you will not believe that a human being is able to create.<br />So, so good. This story is one of my favorites from King's works - action, drama, suspense, unbearable tension, believable character motivations, a unique idea and a wonderfully interesting plot - "The Ledge" has everything a good short story is supposed to have.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>13) The Lawnmover Man</u>
</b> (0/5 stars)<br />Forget it, forget it, forget it.<br />One of the worst short stories ever written. I will introduce zero stars to Goodreads ratings extra for this story.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>14) Quitters, Inc.</u>
</b> (5/5 stars)<br />A middle-aged man wants to quit smoking and visits someone who claims to be able to make him do so. The man doubts these claims - until he realizes whereupon he got himself into ...<br />This short story is perfect; it's as simple as that. No supernatural elements, but instead chilling and suspenseful writing with an ending which made me swallow more than once. Easily one of my favorite short stories of all time. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>15) I Know What You Need</u>
</b> (3,5/5 stars)<br />At university, a young woman meets another man who she falls in love with, not knowing how dangerous this connection may turn out to be.<br />Another very good story. Stephen King knows what he is writing, that's for sure (well, if you ignore certain stories like some of those I've mentioned above). I really liked the complex plot and the hidden appearance of supernatural elements. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>16) Children of the Corn</u>
</b> (3/5 stars)<br />A married couple enters a deserted village with only children inhabiting it - and they clearly have no idea of how to welcome strangers with politeness.<br />Of all the twenty stories in this collection, the one I was most excited about didn't work at all for me. It was scary, yes, scary and thrilling with the religious fanatiscism included, very atmospheric and creepy. Maybe it should have been longer - the potential for a full-length novel was clearly present. Everything felt a little bit too underdeveloped for me.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>17) The Last Rung on the Ladder</u>
</b> (3,5/5 stars)<br />This story deals with the adventures of a young boy and his sister in their childhood. Too short to be really able to explore the characters, but with a surprising twist, a realistic story and suspenseful writing. It's interesting to see how King is able to delve deep into a character's mind within only seven pages. Definitely one of his better stories.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>18) The Man Who Loved Flowers</u>
</b> (2,5/5 stars)<br />It's impossible to say what this story is about without spoiling it. King came up with an interesting concept and an unexpected turn, but on only four pages it was nearly impossible to get into the story. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>19) One for the Road</u>
</b> (4/5 stars)<br />A deserted town. A heavy snowstorm. Vampires lurking in the dark. Sounds like everyone would want to be right in the middle of this scenario, doesn't it?<br />This story creeped me out. It is by far the scariest one in the entire collection. You should avoid reading it in the middle of the night, just like I should have done.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>20) The Woman in the Room</u>
</b> (3/5 stars)<br />A very serious and highly relevant issue portrayed with very weird writing. From a writing point, this story might be worst executed in comparison to all the other stories (if you ignore the Lawnmover Man). It profits from emotion and potential alike.<br /><br /><br />In conclusion, "Night Shift" did not live up to my expectations, but it also didn't disappoint me. Even if you are not interested in Horror or King's writing in general, you should give either "The Ledge" or "Quitters, Inc" a try. Both stories don't include any paranormal activities, but they cover interesting subjects and will keep you on the edge of your seat.<br /><br />It's a must-read for fans of Stephen King's writing and the Horror genre in general, but if you don't consider yourself to belong to one of those parties, then you might think about skipping these stories (apart from "The Ledge" and "Quitters, Inc", of course). But then, with readers raving about this collection everywhere, maybe I'm not the one to trust in this matter ...</span>
  <a data-text-id="12181343215472795820" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2559540845" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4184448375257812380">This is a good, creepy collection. As in lots of short story books, he seemed to place the best ones towards the end. My favorites are the ones that have no supernatural elements at all: "The Ledge", The Last Rung on the Ladder", The Man Who Loved Flowers and the very last story, The Woman in the Room". King is a king of the horror and devastation we feel in real life and that is plenty scary.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1875850753" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1875850753" />
    <a title="Johann (jobis89)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50893023-johann-jobis89"><img alt="Johann (jobis89)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588540681p2/50893023.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1875850753?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Johann (jobis89)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Johann (jobis89)" href="/user/show/50893023-johann-jobis89">Johann (jobis89)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/26164010-night-shift">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50893023-johann-jobis89?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1875850753" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2530339818410885946">"Let's talk, you and I. Let's talk about fear."<br/><br/>Night Shift was Stephen King's first short story collection, released way back in 1978 and it contains quite a lot of his more popular short stories that ended up becoming movies. The prime examples being Children of the Corn and Sometimes They Come Back.<br/><br/>King is often hailed as the master of the short story. Prior to this collection I had only read Nightmares & Dreamscapes and The Bazaar of Bad Dreams, and I did really enjoy them, but found it odd w</span>
  <span id="freeText2530339818410885946" style="display:none">"Let's talk, you and I. Let's talk about fear."<br /><br />Night Shift was Stephen King's first short story collection, released way back in 1978 and it contains quite a lot of his more popular short stories that ended up becoming movies. The prime examples being Children of the Corn and Sometimes They Come Back.<br /><br />King is often hailed as the master of the short story. Prior to this collection I had only read Nightmares &amp; Dreamscapes and The Bazaar of Bad Dreams, and I did really enjoy them, but found it odd when people would comment things like "Oh it was good, but it was disappointing compared to earlier ones". Well, now I get it, guys! Now I get it. You can quite literally feel King's hunger for story-telling throughout the entirety of this collection and given these stories were written at the very start of his career, the material is all so fresh with absolutely amazing, outrageous ideas.<br /><br />I feel like I should reveal that I am not a huge fan of short stories. I want to get lost in a story with the continuing development of a story and its characters. I want to get to know my main characters inside out, back to front. I want to spend days/weeks thinking about the story and the characters and where it's all going, with the anticipation of getting into bed each night to see what happens next. You don't get this with short stories - they're short, that's their nature. You often don't get to find out what happens or why...there's cliffhangers that are never explored again. There isn't that same pull to keep reading and it can take me longer than usual to get through a short story collection. However, Night Shift has completely changed my perspective on short story collections. I WAS thinking about the book all day, but instead wondering what crazy story King has coming next. I DID have the same urge to keep reading. Some characters were memorable, even though I only got to know them for 30 pages or so. This collection was simply out of this world.<br /><br />I almost don't know where to start reviewing this book, but I guess I can start with my absolute favourites in the collection. I can quite honestly say that there was not a bad story in this entire collection, but the much-anticipated Children of the Corn was as impressive as I imagined and is probably the greatest highlight for me. It was creepy and unsettling and even more terrifying than I could have predicted! Sometimes They Come Back was also a great story, alongside I Am The Doorway, The Mangler, Grey Matter, The Lawnmower Man...okay, I think I'm actually starting to list every single story in the book.<br /><br />The Last Rung on the Ladder was also surprisingly emotional and almost brought a tear to the eye. Only King could evoke such a reaction in such a short story. I had previously read One for the Road as it was included in my edition of 'Salem's Lot, but it was great to read this story again. The only problem is...it makes me want to revisit 'Salem's Lot!!<br /><br />Some stories were downright hilarious and just a joy to read, such as Battleground and The Ledge. It's difficult to even pinpoint my least favourite, but if I absolutely had to chose, I'd probably pick The Man Who Loved Flowers - but even then, I really enjoyed this story. It's unusual to not be able to find a flaw in a short story collection, but I've tried and I literally can't.<br /><br />Definitely my top SK short story collection so far!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2530339818410885946" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2327194801" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2327194801" />
    <a title="Jamie Stewart" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15954768-jamie-stewart"><img alt="Jamie Stewart" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551013124p2/15954768.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2327194801?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jamie Stewart" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jamie Stewart" href="/user/show/15954768-jamie-stewart">Jamie Stewart</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2327194801&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2327194801" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer25163872736406847">I used to struggle with the way short story collections can change in tone from one story to the next. That being said I developed a love for that experience as I’ve grown older, which has lead me to discover a wealth of fiction by Stephen King that I haven’t read yet. Night Shift for me is a solid five star collection and the ones that stood out are as follows:<br/><br/><br/>Jerusalem’s Lot - 4.5 Stars - A Lovecraft inspired tale set in Salem’s Lot long before it ever heard of such things as vampires. I hated</span>
  <span id="freeText25163872736406847" style="display:none">I used to struggle with the way short story collections can change in tone from one story to the next. That being said I developed a love for that experience as I’ve grown older, which has lead me to discover a wealth of fiction by Stephen King that I haven’t read yet. Night Shift for me is a solid five star collection and the ones that stood out are as follows:<br /><br /><br />Jerusalem’s Lot - 4.5 Stars - A Lovecraft inspired tale set in Salem’s Lot long before it ever heard of such things as vampires. I hated this story as a teenager because the writing was so different from King’s usually style. As an adult I loved it and found myself properly creeped out. <br /><br />Graveyard Shift - 3 Stars - This is one nasty piece of work in the best possible ways.<br /><br />I Am The Doorway - 5 Stars - Horror fiction rarely scares me but this did. I Am The Doorway features some great body horror and utilises a genre that King rarely writes in, science fiction. Ray Bradbury at his most perverse. <br /><br />The Boogeyman - 5 Stars - An excellent executed tale about a not so nice guy that has one creepy ending. <br /><br />Grey Matter - 3.5 Stars - It’s a story about a contaminated beer can that turns a man into a monster. <br /><br />Trucks - 3 Stars - Vehicles take on a mind of their own and the end of the world ensues. <br /><br />Strawberry Spring - 5 Stars - This one had a Jack the Ripper vibe to me. I loved the writing in this story. Like Jerusalem’s Lot it’s different from King’s usually style in a trippy LSD type of way. <br /><br />The Ledge - 4 - In this story you can see King’s love of wise guys, gangsters and hard-boiled stories. <br /><br />Children of the Corn - 5 Stars - There’s a reason why this short story spawned 7 films. It’s a shame that none of them have come close to the power of this tale. <br /> <br />The Last Rung on the Ladder - 5 Stars - This is not a horror story, but a story of heartache and sorrow. It showcase King’s range and works as a nice prelude for his novella collection Different Seasons. <br /><br />One For The Road - 5 Stars - King returns to Salem’s Lot again and in someways this is even better than his fantastic novel because in its short length it contains everything a readers wants on a horror tale about vampires in winter.</span>
  <a data-text-id="25163872736406847" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
